  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_75d95d03-ada5-4441-98b1-ddbf0e6532a8'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

      initAppleId();

      initializeSiwa();

<span id="freeTextContainer17314954171824248663"><b>“The perfect kind of high-pressure adventure.” —TeenVogue.com<br/>A <i>New York Times</i> bestseller!</b><br/><br/><i>Red Queen</i> meets <i>The Hunger Games</i> in this epic novel about what happens when a senator’s daughter is summoned to the galactic court as a hostage, but she’s really the galaxy’s most dangerous weapon in disguise.<br/><br/><i>A Diabolic is ruthless. A Diabolic is powerful. A Diabolic has a single task:</i></span>
  <span id="freeText17314954171824248663" style="display:none"><b>“The perfect kind of high-pressure adventure.” —TeenVogue.com<br />A <i>New York Times</i> bestseller!</b><br /><br /><i>Red Queen</i> meets <i>The Hunger Games</i> in this epic novel about what happens when a senator’s daughter is summoned to the galactic court as a hostage, but she’s really the galaxy’s most dangerous weapon in disguise.<br /><br /><i>A Diabolic is ruthless. A Diabolic is powerful. A Diabolic has a single task: Kill in order to protect the person you’ve been created for.</i><br /><br />Nemesis is a Diabolic, a humanoid teenager created to protect a galactic senator’s daughter, Sidonia. The two have grown up side by side, but are in no way sisters. Nemesis is expected to give her life for Sidonia, and she would do so gladly. She would also take as many lives as necessary to keep Sidonia safe.<br /><br />When the power-mad Emperor learns Sidonia’s father is participating in a rebellion, he summons Sidonia to the Galactic court. She is to serve as a hostage. Now, there is only one way for Nemesis to protect Sidonia. She must become her. Nemesis travels to the court disguised as Sidonia—a killing machine masquerading in a world of corrupt politicians and two-faced senators’ children. It’s a nest of vipers with threats on every side, but Nemesis must keep her true abilities a secret or risk everything.<br /><br />As the Empire begins to fracture and rebellion looms closer, Nemesis learns there is something more to her than just deadly force. She finds a humanity truer than what she encounters from most humans. Amidst all the danger, action, and intrigue, her humanity just might be the thing that saves her life—and the empire.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17314954171824248663" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      </div>
</div>

          $$('div.prototip').each(function (e) {

              e.setStyle({'display': 'none'});

  <span id="freeText2986589784620598155" style="display:none"><b>Re-read on audio just in time for the second book coming tomorrow on Halloween 2017!! And I still freaking love it! Woot!</b> ❤️<br><br><br>I freaking loved this book!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1446529303ra/16825615.gif" alt=" " class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>All the stars baby!</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1478904626ra/21128051.gif" alt=" " class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I love Nemesis! She is bad @ssed but a really good diabolic and their not supposed to have feelings, goes to show what they know. She is a lethal weapon but she never really liked what she had to do to learn some things. She had to be trained to kill with no hesitation so she could go out in the world and protect another with her life. <br><br><b>The convicts surveyed me, and after a moment, the largest of them broke into a leering grin. "It's just a little girl. I'll do it myself. Come here, girl." He stalked toward me. "You want this bloody or do I just break her neck?"<br><br>"Your choice," the Matriarch said. <br><br>His confidence emboldened the others and set their faces ablaze with the hope of freedom. My heart punched against my rib cage. I had no way to warn them away from me. Even if I had, they would not have listened. Their ringleader had declared me only a girl--and so that was what they saw now. That was their fatal mistake. <br><br>The big one reached down to grab me very carelessly, his hand so close that I could smell his sweat. <br><br>The smell triggered something within me. It was the same as every time before: the fear vanished. Terror dissolved in a swell of rage. <br><br>My teeth clamped down on his hand. Blood spouted, hot and coppery. He shrieked and tried to pull back--too late. I seized his wrist and threw myself forward, twisting his limb as I went. His ligaments crackled. I kicked at the back of his leg to knock him down to the ground. I leaped over him and landed with a stomp of my boots on the back of his head. His skull splintered.</b><br><br>Needless to say it didn't go well for the other two convicts and Nemesis found her a new home to protect, Sidonia, heir to the galactic Senate. <br><br>Sidonia and Nemesis grew up together. Some things happen and then Sidonia's dad does something stupid and other things happen and the evil Emperor wants Sidonia to come to the Imperial Court. Donia's mother has a plan to send Nemesis in her place as no one really knows what anyone looks like through-out the galaxy, they use avatars and what not to talk to each other. They have to train Nemesis to be like a human and they do some drastic and narly stuff to her body. <br><br>When Nemesis arrives she seems to pull it off very well and befriends Neveni a girl from another planet. Seems like the evil Emperor has summoned a lot of heirs and important people to the Imperial Court. <br><br>Then something horrific happens and Nemesis wants to go off on a rampage. But &lt;--she is stopped and saved by the heir of the evil Emperor. His name is Tyrus and I love him and love him and love him. He's the crazy mental relative that no one pays much attention to and he saves Nemesis and things happen and holy crow!!!!! I love him and Nemesis and I love this book and I loved Deadly (&lt;--read the book) and I loved Neveni. Okay so I loved a lot and this book was amazing and I want more, is there going to be more? <br><br>Oh, and I see in some blurbs this book compared to other stuff and NO, it's not like other stuff. It's way better than some of the stuff that it's being compared to and I have no idea why it's even being compared to stuff like that but anyway, this is an awesome sci-fi book and I loved it and I do not care what anyone else thinks =) <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1478904626i/21128052._SX540_.jpg" alt=" : " class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This should be made into a movie. A GOOD movie!! <br> <br>MY BLOG: <a href="http://melissa413readsalot.blogspot.com/2016/11/the-diabolic-by-sj-kincaid.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Melissa Martin's Reading List</a></span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Miranda Reads" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Miranda Reads" href="/user/show/71848701-miranda-reads">Miranda Reads</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2388901898" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1781292615296787235"><blockquote>
<img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1541642639i/26562248._SY540_.jpg' width='400' height='400' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><i>Some might call us a monstrous pair, and they would be right. </i> </blockquote>There is just <b>
  <i>something</i>
</b> absolutely riveting about getting inside the head of a monster.<br/><br/>Nemesis is a Diabolic - a genetically engineered "thing" designed with one, single purpose. She has to keep Sidonia safe - <b>
  <i>at any cost.</i>
</b><br/><br/>Sidonia, the only daughter of a minor nobility, is the absolute <b>light of Nemesis's life. </b>The one thing that holds her grounded and sane.<br/><br/>But Sidonia is not without her quirks - she keeps (stubbornly) insisti</span>
  <span id="freeText1781292615296787235" style="display:none"><blockquote>
<img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1541642639i/26562248._SY540_.jpg" width="400" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>Some might call us a monstrous pair, and they would be right. </i> </blockquote>There is just <b>
  <i>something</i>
</b> absolutely riveting about getting inside the head of a monster.<br><br>Nemesis is a Diabolic - a genetically engineered "thing" designed with one, single purpose. She has to keep Sidonia safe - <b>
  <i>at any cost.</i>
</b><br><br>Sidonia, the only daughter of a minor nobility, is the absolute <b>light of Nemesis's life. </b>The one thing that holds her grounded and sane.<br><br>But Sidonia is not without her quirks - she keeps (stubbornly) insisting that <b>Nemesis is human,</b> that Nemesis has feelings, emotions and more.<br><br>No matter how much Nemesis protests, Sidonia always clings to that belief.<br><br>And when the Emperor decreed that all Diabolics are too dangerous and must be put down, it is through Sidonia's love that Nemesis is spared.<br><br>When Sidonia is summoned to visit the very heart of the empire as a hostage, Nemesis does the only thing possible - <b>
  <i>she goes in her place.</i>
</b><blockquote>
  <i>The Emperor wishes me to send my innocent little lamb to the slaughter. No. Instead, I'll send him my anaconda.</i>
</blockquote> Suddenly, Nemesis has to do the one thing that frightens her most - become human.<blockquote>
  <i>It’s terrifying to realize your own decisions are shaping your destiny.</i>
</blockquote><b>Ooooo! This one gave me <i>shivers.</i></b><br><br> I absolutely LOVED everything about Nemesis. <br><br>She was ruthless and absolutely cutthroat and yet, her sisterly love towards Sidonia and her budding personality really <b>made her shine.</b><br><br>I loved the world that S.J. Kincaid created - all of the nobility scattered across the universe, stubbornly clinging to the past.<blockquote>
  <i>Our ancestors sought knowledge, but we, their descendants, glorify ignorance.</i>
</blockquote>Absolutely cannot wait to get my hands on the sequel! <blockquote>
  <i>I would not just disappear into a void as though I'd never existed. I would not accept that I was less than these people just because they'd designed me that way.</i>

<div id="review_1668219606" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1668219606" />
    <a title="C.G. Drews" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11375137-c-g-drews"><img alt="C.G. Drews" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1521552918p2/11375137.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1668219606?book_show_action=true">Nov 13, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="C.G. Drews" class="user" itemprop="url" name="C.G. Drews" href="/user/show/11375137-c-g-drews">C.G. Drews</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=read-2016">read-2016</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1668219606" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12351462276857141431"><b>This was very stabby and I LIKED IT.</b> Because, well, I have a small love for all things stabtastic (shh, that's a word) and I loved how we got an actual <i>vicious</i> protagonist here who is all anti-hero and inhumane tendencies and stunted emotions and fantastic at stabbing things and WOW, I JUST REALLY ENJOYED THIS. Although <b>I do not like one of the finale plot twists</b> because #illogical. But pfft. Will I let a few small cantankerous feelings put me off? NO I SHALL NOT. GOOD BOOK IS GOOD.<br/><br/>Also you get </span>
  <span id="freeText12351462276857141431" style="display:none"><b>This was very stabby and I LIKED IT.</b> Because, well, I have a small love for all things stabtastic (shh, that's a word) and I loved how we got an actual <i>vicious</i> protagonist here who is all anti-hero and inhumane tendencies and stunted emotions and fantastic at stabbing things and WOW, I JUST REALLY ENJOYED THIS. Although <b>I do not like one of the finale plot twists</b> because #illogical. But pfft. Will I let a few small cantankerous feelings put me off? NO I SHALL NOT. GOOD BOOK IS GOOD.<br /><br />Also you get a list review. AREN'T YOU PLEASED? (Spoiler: you are pleased.)<br /><br /><b>L I K E S: </b><br /><br />• <b>It's set in space!</b> I don't read a lot of sci-fi so this was actually quite exciting! I always love these futuristic settings where they mix sort of an ancient Imperial court (kind of Roman? Greek?) with modern technology and spaceships. It's like ANCIENT GOODNESS IN OUTER SPACE and I like that.<br />• <b>And like I said: stabby.</b> It's actually vicious! I mean, blood doesn't fly everywhere, but the characters don't hold back!<br />• <b>Nemesis is an adorable deadly cinnamon roll.</b> She's a genetically engineered weapon, made as like a permanent bodyguard for her mistress, Donia. All Nemesis wants in life is to PROTECT HER DARLING DONIA. She's like a total robot most of the time....exceeeeeept: she secretly has feelings. And she secretly starts feeling more human. AND SHE'S SECRETLY AWESOME. I loved <b>how the book made her fiercely loving and also robotic at the same time</b>. It didn't make Nemesis unrelatable. In fact, I related to her a lot! It was so easy to root for her while she was simultaneously vicious and loving. She is definitely a new favourite protagonist for me!!<br /><b>• HELLO MIND GAMES!!!</b> Omg I <i>love</i> mind games. And this is full of plot twists, mind games amongst the Emperor and his backstabbing family, and plots and conspiracies. YAS.<br /><b>• Speaking of which: hello to the Emperor's nephew, Tyrus.</b> He's rather mad and I really loved how clever he also was. And he wasn't exactly nice all the time. And I know I seem psychotic to be sitting here saying "Ooh yay mean characters!" but they were mean-characters-I-could-root-for-because-they-loved-fiercely-and-stabbed-just-as-fiercely.<br />• MY PEOPLE.<br />• <b>Also there is a super cute dog!!</b> And by "cute" I mean it was an ugly brute and Nemesis, aka "cold hearted and unfeeling", was an absolute <i>marshmallow</i> to her dog. I LOVE THIS. SO MUCH CUTE.<br />• <b>It was exciting!</b> Always good news for an action adventure story! But I always get cautious when books are set in imperial courts because it can tend to end in dull teaparties. Never fear. There are plenty of dear-death and total-death experiences and the occasional nice dance where my OTP threatens to break each other's necks. Which leads me to...<br /><b>• YES I SHIP IT.</b> Tyrus and Nemesis are damaged, slightly evil, totally poisonous, and fiercely good underneath all that. THESE are the kind of characters I love reading about.<br /><br /><br /><b> D I S L I K E S:</b><br />• <b>It did vaguely feel like a huge mash up.</b> Look there's nothing new out there! But when you've read a loooooot of books (aka me) you start to feel rather unsurprised by things. Basically this book has a LIST of things it reminds me of. For instance: <br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16069030.The_Winner_s_Curse__The_Winner_s_Trilogy___1_" title="The Winner's Curse (The Winner's Trilogy, #1) by Marie Rutkoski" rel="nofollow noopener">The Winner's Curse</a> = Grecian/Roman setting with politics and mind games written in a similar style to The Diabolic<br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/20950716.Spark__Spark___1_" title="Spark (Spark, #1) by Rachael Craw" rel="nofollow noopener">Spark</a> = genetically modified people designed specifically to protect other people<br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15839976.Red_Rising__Red_Rising___1_" title="Red Rising (Red Rising, #1) by Pierce Brown" rel="nofollow noopener">Red Rising</a> = Grecian/Roman setting with the stabby aspects, plus the carving/changing of people's bones and things<br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2767052.The_Hunger_Games__The_Hunger_Games___1_" title="The Hunger Games (The Hunger Games, #1) by Suzanne Collins" rel="nofollow noopener">The Hunger Games</a> = Capitol fashion and amusement tastes + dictatorship that benevolently kills the lower class<br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22328546.Red_Queen__Red_Queen___1_" title="Red Queen (Red Queen, #1) by Victoria Aveyard" rel="nofollow noopener">Red Queen</a> = backstabbing royal family + sci-fi elements<br /><br />I mean, OKAY THAT'S A LOT. And books aren't ever going to be fully original, right?? But as I was reading I couldn't help going "Yeah I saw that plot twist in Red Queen" and "Oh that's exactly what they did with changing people's bone structure in Red Rising"....and it was a bit off putting.<br /><b>The romance did confuse me.</b> There were a lot of "I love yous" being thrown around and I'm like relatively certain Donia was a lesbian and loved Nemesis romantically??? But I wasn't sure??? Because Nemesis didn't seem to love her back anything more than platonically. So possibly it was ALL platonic love, but. I CONFUSED.<br />• <b>DOG DOG DOG.</b> Because <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[the freaking dog GOT MURDERED and I am THIS CLOSE to just slamming a book that ever mentions a dog shut and throwing it across the galaxy BECAUSE STAHP KILLING THE DOGS, YOU MONSTER AUTHORS. STAHP STAHP STAPH. *throws self weeping to the ground. And no. I am not okay. If you wondered. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br />• <b>The plot twist at the end WAS SO ANNOYING.</b> Arghghgh. It's literally grating me to pieces. If I was a piece of cheese, I would be grated so finely you could spread me on your pasta sauce and rename me parmasen sprinkles. AHEM ANYWAY. You get the point. Not happy. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[It was just so <b>freaking obvious that the evil empress was lying.</b> I mean, DUH?!?!??! Nemesis KNOWS she's a rat, she KNOWS the empress wants everyone dead, particularly her annoying nephew. This has been established the WHOLE BOOK. But then at the very end when Donia is murdered by poison and the empress is like "Oh Tyrus is behind this" and Nemesis just <i>believes her straight away???</i> I don't buy it. In fact, it was annoyingly dumb. I couldn't believe Nemesis just swallowed it so easy. Like yeah, trust your enemy and hate your lover FOR NO GOOD REASON AT ALL YOU TWIT. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><b>ALL IN ALL: Yesss I like this one!</b> It wasn't perfect for me, and I did get annoyed at the illogical ending plot twist. But like mind games? Stabbing? Starships? Conspiracies to take down an empire? Forbidden romance? Inhuman characters finding their emotional sides?? (Of which that is my favourite trope, okay.) And an EPIC finale that leaves me wanting more?? Plus a ship that is totally unstable and dangerous and deadly and lovely??? THIS JUST TICKS SO MANY GOOD BOXES FOR ME. I'M NOTORIOUSLY PLEASED.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12351462276857141431" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1713047048" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1713047048" />
    <a title="Cristina Monica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica"><img alt="Cristina Monica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589617514p2/14596170.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1713047048?book_show_action=true">Jul 29, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cristina Monica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cristina Monica" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica">Cristina Monica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=love-triangle">love-triangle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=unrequited-love">unrequited-love</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=bad-romance">bad-romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1713047048" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13848738625217207555">I couldn’t help but repeatedly scrunch up my nose as I was reading <em>The Diabolic. </em><br/><br/>It’s ridiculously brutal and annoyingly unsatisfying.<br/><br/>People die like petty, unimportant flies. No one even bats an eye, or so. I hated it. Normally, I only raise an eyebrow and then carry on (depending on who is dying) but the deaths in this book are revolting.<br/><br/><em>Come on</em>, I get that this is a standalone and that, technically, the author can do whatever she wants with the cast since there will not be any sequels, but to</span>
  <span id="freeText13848738625217207555" style="display:none">I couldn’t help but repeatedly scrunch up my nose as I was reading <em>The Diabolic. </em><br /><br />It’s ridiculously brutal and annoyingly unsatisfying.<br /><br />People die like petty, unimportant flies. No one even bats an eye, or so. I hated it. Normally, I only raise an eyebrow and then carry on (depending on who is dying) but the deaths in this book are revolting.<br /><br /><em>Come on</em>, I get that this is a standalone and that, technically, the author can do whatever she wants with the cast since there will not be any sequels, but to me it felt like most of the killings were only happening to fill plots holes.<br /><br />And that is enraging, especially since one of the characters who die (in quite a merciless way) is so, so sweet and I was even considering rounding my star-rating to three instead of two for them.<br /><br />So now that I’m calm, I’m going to proceed with talking about the other elements. The world-building, to be honest, seemed very interesting in the beginning. I was curious about the ''Diabolics,'' more precisely the roles they had to play. But here again, something happens… and my interest dwindled a little.<br /><br />Aside from that, giving names to places and people does not constitute a world-building. Though, perhaps, it is simply me who finds life in space dreadfully boring, unless there are gigantic slides and pools and hotels hovering above the Earth, or something. But nothing like that here.<br /><br />The romance is horribly unromantic. It’s also so <em>expected, </em>so I really wish the author had done things differently, especially since there is a <em>huge </em>case of unrequited love for one of the characters, and it made me feel sad. The love-interest aren't bad, but they're just so… unoriginal.<br /><br />What kept me going, kept me on reading, was the heroine herself – Nemesis. I swear, if <em>she </em>had died, I would have trashed this book like never seen before. I would have been so, so mad. Fortunately, that does not happen. She is strong and there is real developed in her personality and values. I enjoyed her. Seeing her reactions to what was unknown to her was diverting. She always surprised me.<br /><br />But sadly, loving her is not enough of a reason to concern myself with the future of this world. It can burst into flames, for all I care.<br /><br /><a href="https://hitormissbooks.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/LolaReviewer" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a>Twitter</a> | <a>Instagram</a> | <a href="https://plus.google.com/u/0/105021852309973899120/posts" rel="nofollow noopener">Google+</a> | <a href="https://www.bloglovin.com/blogs/hit-miss-books-12564715" rel="nofollow noopener">Bloglovin’</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="13848738625217207555" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1814763137" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1814763137" />
    <a title="Chelsea Humphrey" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/47207032-chelsea-humphrey"><img alt="Chelsea Humphrey" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1585613513p2/47207032.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1814763137?book_show_action=true">Mar 05, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chelsea Humphrey" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chelsea Humphrey" href="/user/show/47207032-chelsea-humphrey">Chelsea Humphrey</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781481472678" href="/book/show/28953922-the-diabolic">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1814763137" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17610860845459601451">That cover is shiny and gorgeous, right? It’s initially what made me start oogling this book from afar and keeping it on my radar for months before finally taking the time to read and review it. I finally had a legit excuse to jump on the bandwagon once my Literary Box copy arrived, and while I’ll go into more detail below, I was so grateful I chose to read their copy with the author’s notes inside. This detail made the difference in my final star rating, which I decided to round up to a 4 on Go</span>
  <span id="freeText17610860845459601451" style="display:none">That cover is shiny and gorgeous, right? It’s initially what made me start oogling this book from afar and keeping it on my radar for months before finally taking the time to read and review it. I finally had a legit excuse to jump on the bandwagon once my Literary Box copy arrived, and while I’ll go into more detail below, I was so grateful I chose to read their copy with the author’s notes inside. This detail made the difference in my final star rating, which I decided to round up to a 4 on Goodreads in case you don’t follow me there. While I did find some inconsistencies and had a few issues, overall this was a highly enjoyable read! I think what had me flipping back and forth was knowing this is yet <i>ANOTHER</i> YA fantasy series in a sea of YA fantasy series and initially it’s what caused me to pause before picking this up to begin with. To it’s credit, this book was much more engaging and enjoyable than I was anticipating from the reviews I read early on; it’s clearly a book that has encouraged healthy debate which I’m always glad to see.<br /><br /><i>“Did he who made the lamb make thee?”<br />-<b>William Blake</b>, “The Tiger”</i><br /><br /> Let’s start at the very beginning. I really appreciated the immediate insight we receive into just who and what a diabolic is. We learn early on that our narrator is called Nemesis and that all diabolics receive fun, intimidating names, such as Enmity, Hazard, and Anguish. These beings are not human and are created for the sole purpose of bonding with an owner, meaning they form a connection to protect only that one human at any and all costs. After we fast forward a bit to present day, there was a good chunk of the book (about 75 pages I’d say) with a great info dump to catch us up to speed. I struggle with these as they have become a staple in most YA Fantasy fiction; the first in the series contains infamous info dump instead of slowly building it into the story. I think this is just a personal peeve of mine, as it’s clearly up to the author to do as they choose and I know a good number of readers who love this aspect and want to gain the world building knowledge as quickly as possible. Once I got through those pages though, I couldn’t put this down! It was exciting, and fun, and had plenty of twists I didn’t see coming, especially in the final 25%. I greatly appreciate the great dedication to detail and complex layering Kincaid went to in order to ensure the story was necessary in an already saturated market.<br /><br /><i>“Ages ago, humans beings progressed technologically at an exponential rate. We expanded into space; we left Earth and traveled the galaxy. And then the same thing happened that always does-we grew lazy. We had technology we stopped learning how to use. We let machines think for us, act for us. The supernova and rise of the Helionic faith merely worsened a problem that already existed. <b>Our ancestors sought knowledge, but we, their descendants, glorify ignorance.</b>“</i><br /><br />That above was my favorite quote from the entire book. Ok, so we don’t have machines taking over like in <i>The Terminator</i>, but how easily we could apply that last bit to today’s time. I always enjoy a plot that involves the banning of books and knowledge; this was a seed that was planted and investigated in this first book that I’m really hoping is more fleshed out in the following chapters of the trilogy. Even if it comes in an allegorical form, how important is it for us to take a step back and recognize how easy it is for us to become lazy with our technology and our need to make sure our learning never ceases. This book was progressive in many ways, but especially in the sense that women and men have equal chances of ruling and flourishing in leadership roles. I wouldn’t say this novel had huge amounts of diversity, but I would chalk that up to the fact that people altered their appearance for basically every scene, as this was part of their culture. The romance was fairly strong and there wasn’t the typical, dreaded love triangle, although there were a few twists in that department and the ending left me wondering who we can trust and how this story will end in the long run. There was a bit of poetic justice that I appreciated for including a bit of diversity in the love department as well. <i>*Insert vague intrigue here!*</i><br /><br />I think my only major issue with the plot is in the description above on the book jacket, so not a spoiler. We know going into the book that Nemesis and her diabolic kind are incapable of emotions, feelings, etc, yet Nemesis finds herself developing all of those things. We are literally pounded over the head for 150 pages with “I am not capable of feelings or love. I am programmed like a robot.” And then boom, out of nowhere Nemesis has feelings and emotions like it happened overnight. <b>Why? How?</b> None of this was really described or explained. Again, maybe this will be further explored in the remaining entries, but I was slightly bummed that I’m told for half the book one thing and then there is an immediate 180 that I was expected to believe without questioning.<br /><br />The reason I decided to go with a 4 instead of 3 star rating on Goodreads was simply due to the influence the author’s notes had over me. For those who missed it, I was sent a YA review crate from The Literary Box by Quarterly Co. that included this book in it. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4792223.S_J__Kincaid" title="S.J. Kincaid" rel="nofollow noopener">S.J. Kincaid</a> was this quarter’s curator, meaning her book was featured, along with 2 books of her choosing, and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/33480824.The_Diabolic" title="The Diabolic by S.J. Kincaid" rel="nofollow noopener">The Diabolic</a> came full of post it notes with her personal annotations inside. After experiencing this form of reading, I wish I could pick up all my books this way! I cannot stress how insanely pleasing it was to have insider information that other readers didn’t get to experience. I was able to hear out her explanations of why she chose to write things a certain way, what her family’s reactions were to certain plot points, and how things were re-written to keep certain people alive and kill off those initially meant to not die. Sorry, if you want in to you’ll have to order the box, but I highly recommend doing so! Overall, this was a strong start to the series that I only think I’ll grow more fond of as I continue on.<br /><br /><b>*Many thanks to Alinn for providing my box for review; it’s been a pleasure sifting through it and reviewing the products!<br /><br /><i>** In case you missed my initial review of the unveiling of The Lit Box I was sent, you can find that review here:</i> <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://thesuspenseisthrillingme.com/2017/02/24/the-literary-box-ya-edition/">https://thesuspenseisthrillingme.com/...</a> </b></span>
  <a data-text-id="17610860845459601451" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="booksnpenguins" class="user" itemprop="url" name="booksnpenguins" href="/user/show/66222749-booksnpenguins">booksnpenguins</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/66222749-booksnpenguins?shelf=book-heaven">book-heaven</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/66222749-booksnpenguins?shelf=dystopian-and-scifi">dystopian-and-scifi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/66222749-booksnpenguins?shelf=space-and-aliens">space-and-aliens</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1953094848" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15315620129564999578">THIS BOOK THIS BOOK THIS BOOK THIS BOOK THIS BOOK THIS BOOK THIS BOOK THIS BOOK <b>THIS BOOK HOLY CROW THIS BOOK</b><br/><a href='https://gifyu.com/image/LgfT' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1518026687ra/25021409.gif' alt='tumblr_o8kkbhE8QV1tq4of6o1_500.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1585673329i/29206385.png' width='80' height='80' alt='Professional Reader' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1585673329i/29206386.png' width='80' height='80' alt='10 Book Reviews' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1585673329i/29206384.png' width='80' height='80' alt='Reviews Published' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/></span>

    <a title="may ❀" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/49148508-may"><img alt="may ❀" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1562443036p2/49148508.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

<span id="freeTextContainer15139574864217098671"><br/><br/>I am scrolling up and down through <i> The Diabolic </i> reviews and seeing <b> lots </b> of strange things:<br/><br/><b> 4 and 5 star ratings ?????<br/><br/>Average of 4.07 rating from almost 3000 reviews ???? </b><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1484456162ra/21720165.gif' width='400' height='' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Excuuuuuuse me, ARE WE READING THE SAME BOOK???<br/><br/><br/><i> The Diabolic </i> takes place in a sci-fi world where <i> Diabolics </i> are created and chosen to protect their master. <i> Nemesis, </i> our MC, lives to protect and love and care solely for the Senator’s daughter, Sidonia. But when the power-hungry Emperor demands Sidonia as hostage for her f</span>
  <span id="freeText15139574864217098671" style="display:none"><br><br>I am scrolling up and down through <i> The Diabolic </i> reviews and seeing <b> lots </b> of strange things:<br><br><b> 4 and 5 star ratings ?????<br><br>Average of 4.07 rating from almost 3000 reviews ???? </b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1484456162ra/21720165.gif" width="400" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Excuuuuuuse me, ARE WE READING THE SAME BOOK???<br><br><br><i> The Diabolic </i> takes place in a sci-fi world where <i> Diabolics </i> are created and chosen to protect their master. <i> Nemesis, </i> our MC, lives to protect and love and care solely for the Senator’s daughter, Sidonia. But when the power-hungry Emperor demands Sidonia as hostage for her father’s actions, Nemesis is offered in place – hidden in Sidonia’s identity. <br><br>So this book sounds <i> soooooo </i> promising, right?? I mean, I wasn’t a huge advocate of sci-fi fantasy but ever since I read and fell in love with the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23395680.Illuminae__The_Illuminae_Files___1_" title="Illuminae (The Illuminae Files, #1) by Amie Kaufman" rel="nofollow noopener">Illuminae</a> series, I’ve been more open to the genre. <br><br>And then I realized it was filled with books like this. :)<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1484456162ra/21720166.gif" width="400" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The writing is dull. It is monotone and really disconnects the reader from the narrator. I found it incredibly hard to get into this book and ended up skimming at least 75% of it. <br><br>And while there were <i> some </i> <s> very few actually </s> redeeming factors like the plot twists and the <s> small bits of </s> action that we got to read about, it wasn’t enough to save the story. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1396458544ra/9136616.gif" width="400" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br><b> <u> Minor </u> Spoilers ahead </b><br><br>So Nemesis is supposed to be this soul-less monster who cannot fathom emotions or see beyond her need to protect Sidonia. That’s really great, endearing even, but then we go on to find out that Nemesis will fall in love ?????!!!!?????<br><br>W H A T ????<br><br>She’s supposed to be a genetically engineered creature and all of a sudden she has emotions ????<br><br>Where is all this coming from?????<br><br>I feel like this entire book could have been 110% more interesting if the entire romance factor was <b> removed </b> because honestly it’s the most prominent theme throughout the book. <br><br><br>I really hoped for better than this. Needless to say, I will <b> not </b> be continuing the series. <br><br><br><i> “A Diabolic is ruthless. A Diabolic is powerful. A Diabolic has a single task: Kill in order to protect the person you've been created for.” </i><br><br><br>1 star!!<br><br> <br><br><s> <i> BR with the lovely ladies: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/30813900" rel="nofollow noopener">Amber</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/38586507-shukri" rel="nofollow noopener">Shukri</a>, and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/26402455-sana-khalid" rel="nofollow noopener">Sana</a> everyone ditched me rip </i></s> </span>

<div id="review_2199905875" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2199905875" />
    <a title="jessica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10171516-jessica"><img alt="jessica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1509983330p2/10171516.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2199905875?book_show_action=true">Feb 18, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="jessica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="jessica" href="/user/show/10171516-jessica">jessica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781481472685" href="/book/show/34228290-the-diabolic">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2199905875" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer918000571628793134">i had a difficult time writing this review because, within the last six months, ive read two other books with very similar premises and it feels like i will just be repeating what i said in those reviews. so i have tried to stay away from comparisons and just talk about what this particular story did well. <br/><br/>and where this book excels is in its world building. the heart of this story is the galactic kingdoms and various planetary commonwealths. the plot is very politically motivated, so what intri</span>
  <span id="freeText918000571628793134" style="display:none">i had a difficult time writing this review because, within the last six months, ive read two other books with very similar premises and it feels like i will just be repeating what i said in those reviews. so i have tried to stay away from comparisons and just talk about what this particular story did well. <br /><br />and where this book excels is in its world building. the heart of this story is the galactic kingdoms and various planetary commonwealths. the plot is very politically motivated, so what intrigued me most was how highly thought out and cunning the court politics are. everyone has secrets and no character can be trusted, so it was very engaging as a reader to see it all play out from the outside. i think that was the highlight for me. <br /><br />the main component i found to lacking is a strong connection to the characters, and i think that may be a fault of mine rather than the books. there is some character development present and decent introspection, so i dont think thats the problem. i just couldnt bring myself to feel any sort of attachment to any of the characters. no idea why, but i do think i would have enjoyed this much more had i felt anything other than a general sense of apathy. <br /><br />overall, this is an adventurous story with superb world-building and is an excellent set up for what i hope will be an even better sequel! <br /><br /><b>↠ <i>3.5 stars</i></b></span>
  <a data-text-id="918000571628793134" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1848245821" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1848245821" />
    <a title="elena" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/51318038-elena"><img alt="elena" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605725028p2/51318038.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1848245821?book_show_action=true">Dec 24, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="elena" class="user" itemprop="url" name="elena" href="/user/show/51318038-elena">elena</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781481472678" href="/book/show/28953922-the-diabolic">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1848245821" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9643505104690635066"><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>Diabolics weren't people.<br/>We looked like people, to be sure. We had the DNA of people, but we were something else: creatures fashioned to be utterly ruthless and totally loyal to a single individual. We would gladly kill for that person, and only for them.</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br/><br/>When I first read that quote, I thought Nemesis was gonna be loyal so Sidonia, but I was quite wrong. Although I wasn't upset with it, I kind of wished Nemesis would choose Sidonia, but authors sometimes gotta bring other characters </span>
  <span id="freeText9643505104690635066" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>Diabolics weren't people.<br />We looked like people, to be sure. We had the DNA of people, but we were something else: creatures fashioned to be utterly ruthless and totally loyal to a single individual. We would gladly kill for that person, and only for them.</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br /><br />When I first read that quote, I thought Nemesis was gonna be loyal so Sidonia, but I was quite wrong. Although I wasn't upset with it, I kind of wished Nemesis would choose Sidonia, but authors sometimes gotta bring other characters into the story that changes the main character completely or in some ways.<br /><br /><i>The Diabolic</i> is about Nemesis, a diabolic destined to protect one person and only that person. Whoever tries to get near her and hurt her, Nemesis sees them as a target and does whatever she can to kill that person. Sidonia is who Nemesis considers her friend, and is the one she protects. They grew up together, and she is the only person that loves and understands and cares for Nemesis like no other person has. She's her best friend. She's the only person she really has. As the two form a friendship that is inseparable, Nemesis finds out that the Emperor summons Sidonia because of her father's foolish actions - the foolish things he does and stupid actions he takes where he thinks he won't have problems after - and instead of her father paying the price and being in trouble, it's Sidonia. Because Nemesis has been vowed to protect Sidonia, since she would give up her life for Sidonia, Sidonia's mother tells Nemesis that <b>she</b> will be the one to go to the Imperial Court and pretend to be Sidonia to fight and do what the Emperor asks. Nemesis, without arguing, agrees to this.<br /><br /><b>She becomes her.</b><br /><br />When Nemesis arrives at this court, she knows she has to change many things about her including her facial features and expressions, her attitude toward others, and the way she fights is what has to be changed out of everything. She can't give her identity away and she knows she's doing this for Sidonia. She must find her true self in this form that she is in, one including humanity, and must act like one. Humanity might just be the key to saving her people and the Empire, including the people she loves and Nemesis herself.<br /><br />Admittedly, I enjoyed The Diabolic. I'm not really into YA sci-fi/dystopian so I'm not very sure how it should be written and how the world-building should work out, how everything should happen, so I can't say much from my experience. But I will say that I have read some sci-fi that just left me disappointed. It's maybe because the whole dystopian world isn't my kind of thing. It's something I don't really enjoy reading because I don't like reading about people being ruled in this world or having to obey someone that is ruling the dystopian world they live in. I might just have to change that though and begin reading more sci-fi books.<br /><br />So, <b>this book is brutal</b>, to begin with. We're introduced to Nemesis and they want to see what she can do and who she really is, so she proves herself worthy of being able to protect this girl she must protect, Sidonia. From that moment, I knew I would love her character, and I did! She wasn't one of the main characters that leave their place to change their position and become something or someone else, and I was glad of that. She was <b>strong, loyal, determined, and just brutal.</b> Nemesis is one of the best female characters I have met and read about, and that will probably not change. It's just the way she acted around others and how she always made sure her threats were to be kept in their place; how she tried her very best to protect Sidonia and did not fail; how she didn't stop her strength and didn't change her fighting abilities. She was actually a Diabolic; the definition suited her.<br /><br />The story is dystopian since humans and diabolics are completely different although sometimes, it's hard to tell. Diabolics are considered the property and are <i>owned</i> by their owners unless you're like Sidonia where she considered Nemesis her friend, someone she loved and would give up her life like Nemesis would give up hers for her. They are loyal to their "owner" and are faithful to what they say and ask for. They protect them and no matter what happens, they don't dare hurt them. Nemesis was like that. She was only loyal to Sidonia and of course, her parents since she had to, but she protected Sidonia with everything. She made her happy, she made her smile, she made her cry. She didn't change for her or for anyone. Just to summarize it all, <b>Nemesis was a great strong female lead.</b> Even when she knew the circumstances she would get into when she arrived at the court, she knew she was doing this for Sidonia and even when she didn't know where she was and if she was alive or not, she would keep fighting for her because she knew this was what she would do for her. <br /><br />What I <b>did not like</b> about Nemesis was how she was supposed to be this soulless creature that was a ruthless killer to anyone who meant harm to Sidonia but when she met Tyrus, our male lead, she was weak. I mean, she changed for him. Or, she changed in a way. She felt things that she never felt before and she even admitted to herself that she wasn't supposed to be feeling anything, but she did. I read a review and it said their relationship is slow-burn romance, but that's not really true. When Tyrus finds out what Nemesis is, a diabolic, they instantly connect and become one pair, loyal to each other and faithful. You could see the connection they had together, but their relationship formed quick and although I found it cute, I wish it took a little more time for Nemesis to figure things out with Sidonia and Tyrus. I know Sidonia was happy for her because Nemesis was allowing herself to feel things for someone else, but I still wished Nemesis would take time out and figure things out and ask herself questions like <i>"Can I protect both? Can I be with both people? What if I had to make a choice between the two? I love him but I love her?"</i> and even though she told herself she would pick Sidonia over Tyrus, it was hard to believe that since she was questioning herself at times if she really did love Tyrus or if it was normal for her to feel these type of feelings.<br /><br />The male lead who falls in love with our female lead, Tyrus Domitrian, nephew of the Emperor, <b>was pretty bittersweet as we get to read more about him.</b> I expected a little more from him, though. One could see him as a cold-blooded asshole who is ruthless and doesn't care about anyone or anything but when you really get to meet him, you see that he has a very <b>sweet side to Nemesis and would do anything for her.</b> He's also kind of weak, of course, compared to her, that he even decided to train himself with her and would try again and again even when he knew he would lose and he was losing blood and was just in pain. I did like his relationship with Nemesis though and I just found it to be cute. It's weird for me to call it cute, since it's a sci-fi novel, but it's true. I actually thought their relationship was gonna end up like Alina and the Darkling from <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10194157.Shadow_and_Bone__The_Grisha___1_" title="Shadow and Bone (The Grisha, #1) by Leigh Bardugo" rel="nofollow noopener"> Shadow and Bone</a> but luckily, that did not happen. Tyrus was <b>caring</b>, and the way he treated Nemesis even when he knew who and what she was was just so cute! He didn't lie to her in any way even when she thought he did, and he proved himself to be worthy of being his "love". His relationship with her developed in an acceptable manner, although it built up quite quickly.<br /><br />Now, <b>another thing I did not like</b> was how their relationship basically <u>stole</u> the meaning of the book. I mean, Nemesis was being this badass female that would fight for Sidonia but when Tyrus came into her life, the book's elements changed and started forming romance elements, which was something I didn't mind completely. It stole part of the book, since their relationship was forming and as it was, they also had many moments together, alone and in public, but then the sci-fi elements really never died. I said Nemesis didn't change her character, and she didn't. <br /><br />Like I said, one could think he is cold-blooded in the beginning because of how he acts and speaks (how he spoke to Nemesis when she first saw him) but when we get to read more about him and see him in chapters with Nemesis, <b>we see that he's actually sweet and does not want any harm towards anyone, he just wants peace and justice.</b> He and Nemesis had a lot in common, so that was something that fit. They weren't so different that they were a pair that would match. <i>He wanted the throne, and she wanted to kill his uncle, the Emperor.</i> They both basically wished death on the same person and wished for the same thing. He's a precious cinnamon roll and I want him and Nemesis to be happy together and if S.J. Kincaid decides to just, do something to him, well to both but especially to him, I will end up throwing my book and I will find the author and rant and cry after. He deserves happiness since he's never really had it until he met Nemesis. They didn't start off their relationship as enemies and become lovers, but they did start off as a pair that couldn't bare to communicate in a nice way until after.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>Some might call us a monstrous pair, and they would be right. Tyrus and I were both scorpions in our way, dangerous creatures crossing the most treacherous of rivers together. Together we might sting—but we also would float.</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br /><br />Like others have said, the writing in this isn't unique or anything. It wasn't addictive either, I just kept reading because I wanted to see how it would end and what would happen. Something I'm very <b>thankful</b> for is that this did not end in a cliffhanger, which is why I'm surprised it will become a trilogy. At least I don't have to suffer and wait until the next book is published to have questions answered. I'm just imagining Nemesis and Tyrus being happy right now since it ended in a happy moment and I was just satisfied with the ending and very happy as well. This was planned to be a standalone (I think) and I could see why, but I can't see why and how the author decided to make it a trilogy. I'm just wondering what she is planning to do and how she is gonna start off the next book with Nemesis and/or Tyrus.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9643505104690635066" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Shelly Strange" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/25393430-shelly-strange"><img alt="Shelly Strange" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1600285315p2/25393430.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1703117792?book_show_action=true">Jul 19, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Shelly Strange" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Shelly Strange" href="/user/show/25393430-shelly-strange">Shelly Strange</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25393430-shelly-strange?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25393430-shelly-strange?shelf=gurrrl-power">gurrrl-power</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25393430-shelly-strange?shelf=read-2017">read-2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25393430-shelly-strange?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25393430-shelly-strange?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25393430-shelly-strange?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25393430-shelly-strange?shelf=5-stars">5-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25393430-shelly-strange?shelf=this-book-is-everything">this-book-is-everything</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1703117792" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2481071750033435838">I read this for the 2017 <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/148935-dust-off-your-machalo-it-s-time-for-another-buddy-read' rel='nofollow noopener'>MacHalo Group</a> Reading Challenge.<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1506286480i/24003492.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Review:<br/><br/><b>July 5, 2017: One of my favorite books is $1.99 today! If you like space operas with some stabby stabby, pick it up!</b><br/><br/>Please bear with me for a shameless bump. (But this book deserves it!) The most amazing thing happened to me... Someone reached out from <a href='https://quarterly.co/products/literary-young-adult' rel='nofollow noopener'>Quarterly.co</a> about their YA Literary Box. I was offered a sample box that had this book in it! Why in the WORLD would I ever say "no thanks?" Look at what was in it! I'm floored. What</span>
  <span id="freeText2481071750033435838" style="display:none">I read this for the 2017 <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/148935-dust-off-your-machalo-it-s-time-for-another-buddy-read" rel="nofollow noopener">MacHalo Group</a> Reading Challenge.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1506286480i/24003492.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Review:<br><br><b>July 5, 2017: One of my favorite books is $1.99 today! If you like space operas with some stabby stabby, pick it up!</b><br><br>Please bear with me for a shameless bump. (But this book deserves it!) The most amazing thing happened to me... Someone reached out from <a href="https://quarterly.co/products/literary-young-adult" rel="nofollow noopener">Quarterly.co</a> about their YA Literary Box. I was offered a sample box that had this book in it! Why in the WORLD would I ever say "no thanks?" Look at what was in it! I'm floored. What a treasure - and it really came at a time when I needed something special like this. I will keep it forever. It's my precious!!! Thank you so very much, Alinn! <br><br>(And I read and reviewed this awesome book - and actually I read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/764347.Unwind__Unwind___1_" title="Unwind (Unwind, #1) by Neal Shusterman" rel="nofollow noopener">Unwind</a> a LONG time ago - before her most generous offer came around.)<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1488593193i/22134530.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Original post:</b> Well, this was just fantastic. I had no expectations going in, decided to read it at a whim, and what a nice surprise! This is more sci-fi than fantasy and takes place almost entirely in space. You have the typical futuristic dystopian government set up... in this case, there is an Emperor and the lower caste politicians, who are very powerful and treated like royalty. These politicians basically live on huge space station-like ships that have their own habitats in them. They have the technology to remain youthful and live long, med-bots to cure illness and injuries, holographic realities to meet up with people light years away. <br><br>But the society is incredibly gluttonous, amoral, and hedonistic. They have balls and galas where they take drugs and act like petulant adolescents. They have rejected science in favor of a vague space god and everyone has forgotten how to build their ships and repair them. So space is being ravaged in negligence and no one is allowed to do anything about it. Of course, different factions are unhappy about the way things are.<br><br>There are genetically engineered humans (some are used as servants, some are used as musicians, some are used as body guards). The elite do not view them as real or human. They treat them as things, like animals or worse. The Diabolics are top of the line body guards, born and bred to become chemically bonded to one person and protect them until death. They of course have super strength and senses.<br><br>The book is about a Diabolic who discovers her humanity. I thought the author did a great job showing this transformation. Nemesis is her name and she becomes someone you can really root for and feel for.<br><br>There is a romance. I liked it. I could get behind it. <br><br>There are other humans who live on planets and the elite view them as lessers. They think living on a planet is gauche and primitive. <br><br>There is the typical rise up and fight against the tyranny plot. I happen to love books like this and I thought this one had a nice twist and originality.<br><br>I have no issues with this. I would buy a hard copy, I would re-read it. I am definitely going to read the next one. This is exactly what I want in a book. Good story, good pacing, characters you can root for, romance that isn't annoying, twists, a little bit of drama that doesn't drag on, exciting world-building... I have no complaints. So five stars it is.<br><br>Read for the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/148935-dust-off-your-machalo-it-s-time-for-another-buddy-read" rel="nofollow noopener">Machalo</a> group 2017 challenge:<br><br><b>7) Book set in space</b></span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1672723797?book_show_action=true">Jun 18, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Candace Robinson" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Candace Robinson" href="/user/show/33995641-candace-robinson">Candace Robinson</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer1672723797" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer13875640701704701734">First off this is nothing like Red Queen or The Hunger Games. I hate when they try to compare books, and it is totally different. I loved this book, and Nemesis is an MC that was one like I have never read before. She was ruthless and lovable at the same time. I loved seeing her become more human but still maintain her protective stances. Towards the end things get pretty darn intense! Full review on my blog <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='https://literarydust.wordpress.com/2016/08/12/review-the-diabolic-by-s-j-kincaid/'>https://literarydust.wordpress.com/20...</a><br/><br/>I received an awesome hardback copy of this book</span>
  <span id="freeText13875640701704701734" style="display:none">First off this is nothing like Red Queen or The Hunger Games. I hate when they try to compare books, and it is totally different. <div id="review_2216210378" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2216210378" />
    <a title="Jessi ♥️ H. Vojsk" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/66224803-jessi-h-vojsk"><img alt="Jessi ♥️ H. Vojsk" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1597641717p2/66224803.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2216210378?book_show_action=true">Feb 20, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jessi ♥️ H. Vojsk" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jessi ♥️ H. Vojsk" href="/user/show/66224803-jessi-h-vojsk">Jessi ♥️ H. Vojsk</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2216210378" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8786173770447749842"><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1519203918ra/25096884.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><i> “A Diabolic is ruthless. <br/>A Diabolic is powerful. <br/>A Diabolic has a single task: <br/>Kill in order to protect the person you've been created for.” </i> <br/><br/>Story ⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️<br/>Nemesis always thought she was an inhuman machine, a DNA-designed “thing” to protect her beloved Sidonia as a Diabolic. <br/>So when Sidonia is threatened by the Emperor and send to the court of the Emperor, Nemesis secretly goes in her place.<br/>Trying to protect Sidonia and her family Nemesis learns more of humanity by seeing all the friendships, s</span>
  <span id="freeText8786173770447749842" style="display:none"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1519203918ra/25096884.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i> “A Diabolic is ruthless. <br>A Diabolic is powerful. <br>A Diabolic has a single task: <br>Kill in order to protect the person you've been created for.” </i> <br><br>Story ⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️<br>Nemesis always thought she was an inhuman machine, a DNA-designed “thing” to protect her beloved Sidonia as a Diabolic. <br>So when Sidonia is threatened by the Emperor and send to the court of the Emperor, Nemesis secretly goes in her place.<br>Trying to protect Sidonia and her family Nemesis learns more of humanity by seeing all the friendships, skepticism, betrayal and love of humans. <br>In the end the court is full of intrigues and liars. <br>In the beginning I wasn’t really sure If I liked this book. Until Nemesis was send to court this book was a three star book for me. <br>But then she arrived at court and the real fun began. Slowly I was completely in love with Nemesis and her life. <br>Sometimes the book had a slow pacing, but it still was so addictive, that you needed to finish the chapter only to start the next chapter to see what will happen next. <br><br>Characters ⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️<br>As I said I wasn’t really fond of the story in the beginning. I had the same feeling about Nemesis. She was a DNA-created machine and that’s the exact feeling you had while reading.<br>But then she slowly had an amazing and really strong character development throughout the book, so in the end I fell completely in love with her. <br>Then there was also Tyrus - the madman and heir to the Empire. I always have a thing for the “villains” of the story and Tyrus was the perfect example for this type of character. In the end there was more and more revealed of his real and complex personality, so I could actually defend my love for him. <br>Don’t get me wrong, I don’t think Tyrus is a good guy, no, I don’t trust him. Especially in the end. <br>But he was still the most interesting characters of them all. <br><br>World ⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️<br>I’m not a big fan of sci-fi (sorry 🤷🏻‍♀️). Maybe that’s because I haven’t read many sci-fi books I liked. <br>But this book had such a great, wonderful-imagined world in the universe, it could actually change my opinion about sci-fi. <br>I’m not really able to explain the world of Diabolic to you, but let’s just say: there are <br>- medical bots that can cure illnesses and injuries in a few minutes <br>- Beauty bots that can change your whole appearance and make you even younger (or shorter/weaker)<br>- There are Diabolics who are designed to protect certain people <br>- There is a royal family that would make the “game-of-Thrones” author nod in adoration. <br><br>Relationships ⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️<br>Oh man, oh man, how can I tell you about the relationships in this book without spoilering you till the very end? <br>Okay, I can’t. Lets just give you a few hints. <br>First of all I’m absolutely in love with the love story in this book. <br>It was so perfectly imperfect. <br>It was a love that was felt vulnerable, cute and passionate and so much more. <br>But there were also friendships to love, families to fear and people to hate in this book. <br><br>Writing style ⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️<br>The writing wasn’t my favorite, by all means the author won’t become one of my favorite authors. But it was still a good, nice written book that was action filled and had cute (but also really weird) love scenes.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8786173770447749842" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
