  <span id="freeText17606134133264786227" style="display:none">This book totally surprised me. It was the Donald Trump of books because it really <i>grabbed</i> my attention and wouldn't let it go.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1489051814i/22180175.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>*whispers* never let me go...</i><br><br>If you were a fan of Red Rising, you will really like this one. It has the same feel with a fake identity, court &amp; political intrigues, twisty turns, lots of bloody death, and a bunch of insanity. There were so many times when you weren't sure who was trying to kill who. I loved that!<br><br>Our heroine is Nemesis, who is a genetically engineered bodyguard. She protects the daughter of a senator who has pissed off the evil emperor. Because the emperor is so evil, he decides to take the daughter hostage to keep the father in line. Of course, the parents have no intention of sending their daughter to the emperor's court, so they give a makeover to Nemesis and send her in the daughter's place.<br><br>Open the beauty parlor!<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1489051815i/22180178._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>She's going to need that knife at court</i><br><br>The "court" where all the political players are assembled is something out of the Capital from the Hunger Games. Insane style's, complete debauchery, and serious danger. The emperor is a sadistic bastard, so this book isn't for the faint-hearted. There is a lot of cruelty and bloodshed. In other words, it's a lot of fun to read for a bloodthirsty person like myself. :D<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1489051814i/22180177._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>real life picture of me as a youth. Stupid dinosaurs had it coming.</i><br><br>Oh, have I mentioned that all of this is set in space? Yeah! Cool! We have one scene where our girl travels to a planet for the first time and she is absolutely disgusted by all of the germs, messiness, and weather. Also, the sky freaks her out. In other words, a heartless killer is afraid of mosquitoes. And, they aren't even Texas mosquitoes.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1489051814i/22180176.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>We could use them as free public transportation. Well, you do pay. In blood.</i><br><br>I got this book in my cool Birchbox for books package (<a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://quarterly.co/products/literary-young-adult">https://quarterly.co/products/literar...</a>) and it even included a bunch of notes from the author. That part of it was awesome because the insights in those notes made me understand a lot of the choices that were made. I think all authors should give us notes on what they were thinking when they write certain things. Some of them have some 'splainin' to do. (Tris dying? Prim dying? Bella being interesting enough for a book? SMH) <br></span>

<div id="review_2081574578" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2081574578" />
    <a title="Gavin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8192509-gavin"><img alt="Gavin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1338207884p2/8192509.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2081574578?book_show_action=true">Aug 08, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Gavin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Gavin" href="/user/show/8192509-gavin">Gavin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8192509-gavin?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8192509-gavin?shelf=ya-books">ya-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2081574578" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15831636750248554604">I had high hopes for The Diabolic because the blurb grabbed my attention and made it sound like just the sort of sci-fi book I love to read. The actual story definitely delivered on the promise of the blurb. S. J. Kincaid had an engaging writing style and I loved both the characters and the story itself. The world building was a little simplistic but it was effective so it did not hurt the story. <br/><br/>A Diabolic is a genetically engineered human designed to protect the human it is bonded to at all co</span>
  <span id="freeText15831636750248554604" style="display:none">I had high hopes for The Diabolic because the blurb grabbed my attention and made it sound like just the sort of sci-fi book I love to read. The actual story definitely delivered on the promise of the blurb. S. J. Kincaid had an engaging writing style and I loved both the characters and the story itself. The world building was a little simplistic but it was effective so it did not hurt the story. <br /><br />A Diabolic is a genetically engineered human designed to protect the human it is bonded to at all costs. Diabolic are superior to regular humans in every way. They are faster, stronger, and far more resilient than any regular human could hope to be and that is before the training they undergo from creation to hone their deadly skills! Nemesis is a Diabolic. She was created to protect Sidonia, who is the daughter of one of the noble families in the Empire. When Sidonia's father makes some unwise political moves that upset the Emperor, Sidonia is called to the royal court to act as surety of his future good behaviour. Given the Emperor's well know cruel nature it is decided that Nemesis will go to court in the guise of Sidonia!<br /><br />The story was a ton of fun. Nemesis managed to be a super likeable lead character despite being a ruthless killer and it was great following her as she mimicked being a regular human! Her nature made her what she was so it was still easy to root for her and her development from a Diabolic into something more as the story progressed. The secondary characters were an interesting bunch. Sidonia was surprisingly likeable despite her pretty much being Sidonia's owner. When Nemesis pitched up at court we got to meet a whole bunch of interesting villains and a few likeable characters. The best of them turned out to be the Emperor's insane nephew and heir. <br /><br />The sci-fi elements of this story were pretty cool. There was a lot of cool sci-fi technology but the rise of a knowledge opposed religion meant that no one had any deep understanding of how any of the technology worked! <br /><br />All in all I found this a very fast paced and exciting read full of characters than were easy to like and root for and with a story that kept me totally captivated from start to finish. S. J. Kincaid just knew the perfect moment when a surprise twist was needed to keep the tension at a maximum! <br /><br />Rating: An easy 5 stars as this is one of my favourite new YA finds in years.<br /><br />Audio Note: Candace Thaxton gave a fantastic performance in this one. She got the tone of the story and her voice acting was very good. </span>
  <a data-text-id="15831636750248554604" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2165525611" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2165525611" />

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2165525611?book_show_action=true">Oct 27, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Veronica ⭐️" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Veronica ⭐️" href="/user/show/6716390-veronica">Veronica ⭐️</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781471148392" href="/book/show/33541577-the-diabolic">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6716390-veronica?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6716390-veronica?shelf=2017">2017</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2165525611" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13098220882492198715">Wow! I loved this book. It’s fast paced and nasty.<br/>The story is narrated by Nemesis. She is a Diabolic. Bred to protect their bonded human. They have no feelings, no love, fear or empathy, only a fierce loyalty to the person they are bonded to. Only thing is Nemesis has felt fear and empathy, but when it comes down to kill or be killed, she will kill.<br/><br/>Nemesis’ role is to protect Sidonia and when Sidonia’s father, Senator Von Impyrean, displeases the Emperor and Sidonia is summoned to the courts he</span>
  <span id="freeText13098220882492198715" style="display:none">Wow! I loved this book. It’s fast paced and nasty.<br />The story is narrated by Nemesis. She is a Diabolic. Bred to protect their bonded human. They have no feelings, no love, fear or empathy, only a fierce loyalty to the person they are bonded to. Only thing is Nemesis has felt fear and empathy, but when it comes down to kill or be killed, she will kill.<br /><br />Nemesis’ role is to protect Sidonia and when Sidonia’s father, Senator Von Impyrean, displeases the Emperor and Sidonia is summoned to the courts her family send Nemesis in her place.<br /><br />Here we enter a world of beauty bots that can alter, enhance and colour your appearance on a whim. A world where recreational drugs and opiates are an everyday indulgence. A world where you need to tread lightly and watch your back as no-one can be trusted. A world where machines do everything and science and learning are strictly forbidden. A beautiful world of balls and gowns and operas. A savage world where life has no measure and ranking is everything.<br /><br />The Emperor used fear and terror to control his people.<br /><i>” I often think power is the most noxious substance in the universe. Both want and possession of it warp one’s character beyond redemption.”</i> - Grandee Cygna Domitria.<br /><br />S.J. Kincaid has developed a world that is easy to comprehend. There are no great info dumps or complicated political structures. The simplicity of the world makes for an easy enjoyable read.<br /><br />Thank you Kincaid for restoring my faith in the YA genre. I fell in love with Sidonia, Nemesis and Tyrus. I story where the evil are truly heartless but there is also a blurred line between good and bad creating a truly outstanding heroine in Nemesis.<br /><br />I am now looking forward to reading book two “The Empress”.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="13098220882492198715" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('knwHW9XNj2OqGID+6MEPsdHv8P2u0R0ryiJxYS9HqvvHu8RCkF2/O8KUCstvFMIDvGQJas0vyXLZ5+EoLMj2ow==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('mb936rxcfphimRYD4jgpIBRF9/pbMm/jrKmGrXALFrHMeLTz+cxOwAoVnDZl7eSSec4ObTjMu7q/bBbkc4RK6Q==')})
  }
//]]>
